      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n4631-1" target="الثُّلَاثَآء" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, with damm, (A, K,) [meaning <hi rend="ital">The third day of the week, Tuesday,</hi>] has this form for the sake of distinction; for properly it should be <foreign lang="ar">الثَّالِثُ</foreign>: (S, M:) or it has meddeh in the place of the <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> in the noun of number [<foreign lang="ar">ثَلَاثَةٌ</foreign>] to distinguish it from the latter: (Lth, T:) [it is without tenween in every case; when indeterminate as well as when determinate; being fem.:] the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">ثَلَاثَاوَاتٌ</foreign> (S, M, Msb) and <foreign lang="ar">أَثَالِثُ</foreign>. (Th, M.) It has no dim. (Sb, S in art. <foreign lang="ar">امس</foreign>.) Lh relates that Aboo-Ziyád used to say, <foreign lang="ar">مَضَى الثَّلَاثَآءُ بِمَا فِيهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Tuesday passed with what</hi> occurred <hi rend="ital">in it</hi>]; making <foreign lang="ar">ثلاثاء</foreign> sing. and masc.; [but this he did because he meant thereby <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الثَّلَاثَآءِ</foreign>; <foreign lang="ar">يوم</foreign> being masc.:] Th is related to have said, <foreign lang="ar">بِمَا فِيهَا</foreign>; making it fem.: and Abu-l-Jarráh used to say, <foreign lang="ar">مَضَتِ الثَّلَاثَآءُ بِمَا فِيهِنَّ</foreign>, treating the word as a numeral. (M.)    </entryFree>2e:T4e4,<entryFree id="n4633" key="ثُلَاثِىٌّ" type="main">

               </entryFree>30:T179b,<entryFree id="n4638" key="ثَالِثٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ثَالِثٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ثالث</orth>
                  </form> [<hi rend="ital">Third</hi>]: fem. with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>. (T, &amp;c.) The final <foreign lang="ar">ث</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">الثَّالِثُ</foreign> is sometimes changed into <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>. (M.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ ثَالِثُ ثَلَاثَةٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, is the third of three</hi>]: thus you say when the two [terms] agree, each with the other; but not <foreign lang="ar">ثَالِثٌ ثَلَاثَةً</foreign>; <foreign lang="ar">ثالث</foreign> being regarded in the former case as though it were a subst.; for you do not mean to convey by it a verbal signification, but only mean that he, or it, is one of the three, or a portion of the three: (Fr, ISk, T, S:) and in like manner you say, <foreign lang="ar">هِىَ ثَالِثَةُ ثَلَاثَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">She is the third of three</hi>]; but when there is among the females a male, you say, <foreign lang="ar">هِىَ ثَالِثَةُ ثَلَاثَةٍ</foreign>, making the masc. to predominate over the fem. (T.) When the two [terms] are different, you may make the former to govern the gen. case or to govern as a verb; saying, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ رَابِعُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ثَلَاثَةٍ</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ رَابِعٌ ثَلَاثَةً</foreign>, like as you say <foreign lang="ar">ضَارِبُ زَيْدٍ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ضَارِبٌ زَيْدًا</foreign>; and thus you also say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا ثَالِثُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱثْنَيْنِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا ثَالِثٌ ٱثْنَيْنِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">This makes two to be three, with himself,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">itself.</hi> (ISk, T, * S. [In most copies of the S, for <foreign lang="ar">ثَالِثٌ ٱثْنَيْنِ</foreign> is put <foreign lang="ar">ثَالِثَ ٱثْنَيْنِ</foreign>; and, in the explanation of this phrase, <foreign lang="ar">ثَلَّثَ ٱثْنَيْنِ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">ثَلَثَ ٱثْنَيْنِ</foreign>: IB has remarked that these are mistakes.])   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n4638-1" target="ثِلَاث" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n4626"/></foreign> occurs in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">ثَالِث</foreign> in a trad. cited voce <foreign lang="ar">ثَانٍ</foreign> in art. <foreign lang="ar">ثنى</foreign>. (Sh, T in art. <foreign lang="ar">ثنى</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ثَالِثَةُ الأَثَافِى</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">A projecting portion of a mountain, by which are placed two pieces of rock, upon all which is placed the cooking-pot.</hi> (S, K.) Hence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">رَمَاهُ ٱللّٰهُ بِثَالِثَةِ الأَثَافِى</foreign> [explained in art. <foreign lang="ar">اثف</foreign>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">ثَالِثَ عَشَرَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ثَالِثَةَ عَشْرَةَ</foreign>, the former masc. and the latter fem., meaning <hi rend="ital">Thirteenth,</hi> are generally held to be indecl. in every case without the art.; but with the art., most say in the nom. <foreign lang="ar">الثَّالِثُ عَشَرَ</foreign>, accus. <foreign lang="ar">الثَّالِثَ عَشَرَ</foreign>, and gen. <foreign lang="ar">الثَّالِثِ عَشَرَ</foreign>; and in like manner in the fem. Accord. to some,] you say, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ ثَالِثُ عَشَرَ</foreign> as well as <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ ثَالِثَ عَشَرَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, is a thirteenth</hi>]: he who uses the former phrase says that he means <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ ثَالِثُ ثَلَاثَةَ عَشَرَ</foreign>, (T, S,) i. e. <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, is one of thirteen,</hi> (T,) and that he suppresses <foreign lang="ar">ثلاثه</foreign>, and leaves <foreign lang="ar">ثالث</foreign> decl. as it was; and he who uses the latter phrase says that he likewise means this, but that, suppressing <foreign lang="ar">ثلاثة</foreign>, he gives its final vowel to the word <foreign lang="ar">ثالث</foreign>, (T, S,) to show that there is a suppression: (S:) but IB says that the former of these two phrases is wrong; that the Koofees allow it, but that the Basrees disallow it, and pronounce it a mistake. (L.) [And accord. to J, one says, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الثَّالِثَ عَشَرَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">هٰذِهِ الثَّالِثَةَ عَشْرَةَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">This is the thirteenth,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">this thirteenth:</hi> for he adds,] and you say, <foreign lang="ar">هذَا الحَادِى عَشَرَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الثَّانِىَ عَشَرَ</foreign> and so on to twenty [exclusive]; all with fet-h; for the reason which we have mentioned: and in like manner in the fem., in which each of the two nouns is with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>. (S.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">ثَالِثَ عَشَرَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ثَلَاثَةَ عَشَرَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The thirteenth of thirteen</hi>]; and so on to <foreign lang="ar">تَاسِعَ عَشَرَ تِسْعَةَ عَشَرَ</foreign>: and in like manner in the fem.
